<h3><span class="mw-headline" id="Funding">Funding</span><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=Australian_Broadcasting_Corporation&amp;action=edit&amp;section=10" title="Edit section: Funding">edit</a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></h3>
<p>The ABC is funded mainly by the Australian government, in addition to some revenue received from <a href="/wiki/ABC_Commercial" title="ABC Commercial">its retail outlets</a>. In the 2006–07 <a href="/wiki/Australian_federal_budget" title="Australian federal budget">federal budget</a>, the ABC received <a href="/wiki/Australian_dollar" title="Australian dollar">A$</a>823 million of government funding,<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-67"><a href="#cite_note-67">[67]</a></sup> increased to $840 million in 2008–09.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-budgetreport_1-1"><a href="#cite_note-budgetreport-1">[1]</a></sup> In the 2009–10 federal budget, the ABC received funding of $929.9 million.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-68"><a href="#cite_note-68">[68]</a></sup></p>
<p>Until 1948, the ABC was funded directly by radio licence fees; amendments were also made to the <i>Australian Broadcasting Act</i> that meant the ABC would receive its funding directly from the federal government. Licence fees remained until 1973 when they were abolished by the <a href="/wiki/Gough_Whitlam" title="Gough Whitlam">Whitlam</a> Labor government, on the basis that the near-universality of television and radio services meant that public funding was a fairer method of providing revenue for government-owned radio and television broadcasters.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-whoseabc_27-2"><a href="#cite_note-whoseabc-27">[27]</a></sup></p>
<p>The term "where your 8 cents a day goes", coined in the late 1980s during funding negotiations,<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-8cents_69-0"><a href="#cite_note-8cents-69">[69]</a></sup> is often used in reference to the services provided by the ABC.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-70"><a href="#cite_note-70">[70]</a></sup> It is estimated that the cost of the ABC per head of population per day was 7.1 cents a day, based on the Corporation's 2007–08 'base funding' of $543 million.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-71"><a href="#cite_note-71">[71]</a></sup> Budget figures above show the ABC costs over 14 cents per day today.</p>
<p>The Australian Communications Minister, Senator <a href="/wiki/Stephen_Conroy" title="Stephen Conroy">Stephen Conroy</a> indicated strong support from the Government for the ABC's funding submission for the 2009/10 budget, saying the organisation had been underfunded for many years.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-72"><a href="#cite_note-72">[72]</a></sup></p>
<h2><span class="mw-headline" id="Politics_and_criticism">Politics and criticism</span><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=Australian_Broadcasting_Corporation&amp;action=edit&amp;section=11" title="Edit section: Politics and criticism">edit</a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></h2>
<div class="hatnote navigation-not-searchable" role="note">See also: <a href="/wiki/ABC_Board" title="ABC Board">ABC Board</a> and <a href="/wiki/History_of_the_Australian_Broadcasting_Corporation" title="History of the Australian Broadcasting Corporation">History of the Australian Broadcasting Corporation</a></div>
<h3><span class="mw-headline" id="Independence_and_impartiality">Independence and impartiality</span><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=Australian_Broadcasting_Corporation&amp;action=edit&amp;section=12" title="Edit section: Independence and impartiality">edit</a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></h3>
<p>Under the <i>Australian Broadcasting Corporation Act 1983</i>,<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-73"><a href="#cite_note-73">[73]</a></sup> the <a href="/wiki/ABC_Board" title="ABC Board">ABC Board</a> is bound to "maintain the independence and integrity of the Corporation" and to ensure that "the gathering and presentation by the Corporation of news and information is accurate and impartial according to the recognized standards of objective journalism."</p>
<p>In relation to impartiality and diversity of perspectives, the current ABC editorial policy requires of the broadcaster that:<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-74"><a href="#cite_note-74">[74]</a></sup></p>
<blockquote class="templatequote">
<p>... the ABC gather and present news and information with impartiality and presents a diversity of perspectives so that, over time, no significant strand of thought or belief within the community is knowingly excluded or disproportionately represented. The broadcaster is expected to take no editorial stance other than a commitment to fundamental democratic principles.</p>
<div class="templatequotecite">— <cite>ABC Editorial Policy</cite></div>
</blockquote>
<h4><span class="mw-headline" id="Criticisms">Criticisms</span><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=Australian_Broadcasting_Corporation&amp;action=edit&amp;section=13" title="Edit section: Criticisms">edit</a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></h4>
<p>As a publicly funded broadcaster, the ABC is expected not to take editorial stances on political issues, and is required to present a range of views with impartiality. Over the decades, accusations of "bias" at the ABC have arisen at different times, and various inquiries undertaken.</p>
<p>Reviews of the ABC are regularly commissioned and sometimes not released.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-Martin_75-0"><a href="#cite_note-Martin-75">[75]</a></sup><sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-Gordon_76-0"><a href="#cite_note-Gordon-76">[76]</a></sup> A 2004 <a href="/wiki/Roy_Morgan_Research" title="Roy Morgan Research">Roy Morgan</a> media credibility survey found that media professionals regarded <a href="/wiki/ABC_Radio_and_Regional_Content" title="ABC Radio and Regional Content">ABC Radio</a> as the most accurate news source in the country.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-77"><a href="#cite_note-77">[77]</a></sup> In mid 2013 the <a href="/wiki/University_of_the_Sunshine_Coast" title="University of the Sunshine Coast">University of the Sunshine Coast</a> released a study of the professional views of journalists. Slightly over half of respondents expected to vote for either <a href="/wiki/Australian_Labor_Party" title="Australian Labor Party">Labor</a> or <a href="/wiki/Australian_Greens" title="Australian Greens">The Greens</a> whereas just under a third planned to vote <a href="/wiki/Coalition_(Australia)" title="Coalition (Australia)">Coalition</a>. In contrast over 40% of ABC journalists would vote for The Greens and almost a third Labor.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-Hanusch_78-0"><a href="#cite_note-Hanusch-78">[78]</a></sup><sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-79"><a href="#cite_note-79">[79]</a></sup></p>
<p>Dr Rhonda Jolly's 2014 ABC Overview noted that "many commentators have argued consistently that there is a left wing bias which dominates ABC news and programming" and cited a 2005 piece by Paul Gray that the broadcaster was overly influenced by the "narrow middle-class values of the Australian secular Left" and said that "while the national broadcaster had at times offended governments of all persuasions, it had always adopted a 'from the Left' perspective." Jolly also noted however that supporters of the ABC "deny claims that the broadcaster is either intentionally or inadvertently biased" and that "Speaking from opposition, politicians have praised the ABC for its scrutiny of government." The paper noted that, in December 2013, ABC chairman James Spigelman called four independent audits a year in response to the frequent allegations of lack of impartiality in news and current affairs.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-80"><a href="#cite_note-80">[80]</a></sup> In response to one set of criticisms, journalist <a href="/wiki/Annabel_Crabb" title="Annabel Crabb">Annabel Crabb</a>, who has worked at the ABC, commented: "every single day I see that organisation give voices to Australians who otherwise wouldn't be heard, on topics that are too uncommercial or too remote or too hard to be covered by anyone else, broadcasting into areas from which others have long withdrawn resources."<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-81"><a href="#cite_note-81">[81]</a></sup></p>
<h5><span class="mw-headline" id="1960s_and_1970s">1960s and 1970s</span><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=Australian_Broadcasting_Corporation&amp;action=edit&amp;section=14" title="Edit section: 1960s and 1970s">edit</a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></h5>
<p>The conservative <a href="/wiki/Liberal_Party_of_Australia" title="Liberal Party of Australia">Liberal Party</a> governments in the 1960s and 1970s attempted<sup class="noprint Inline-Template" style="margin-left:0.1em; white-space:nowrap;">[<i><a href="/wiki/Wikipedia:Manual_of_Style/Words_to_watch#Unsupported_attributions" title="Wikipedia:Manual of Style/Words to watch"><span title="The material near this tag may use weasel words or too-vague attribution. (April 2016)">according to whom?</span></a></i>]</sup> to influence the ABC's political coverage by threatening to reduce funding for its news and current affairs division.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-mediawedeserve_82-0"><a href="#cite_note-mediawedeserve-82">[82]</a></sup><sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-openseasonabc_83-0"><a href="#cite_note-openseasonabc-83">[83]</a></sup></p>
<h5><span class="mw-headline" id="Hawke-Keating_Government">Hawke-Keating Government</span><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=Australian_Broadcasting_Corporation&amp;action=edit&amp;section=15" title="Edit section: Hawke-Keating Government">edit</a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></h5>
<p><a href="/wiki/Bob_Hawke" title="Bob Hawke">Bob Hawke</a> criticised some of the <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/7.30_Report" title="7.30 Report">7.30 Report</a>'s coverage of the 1991 Gulf War to which he committed naval forces as being "loaded", "biased" and "disgraceful".<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-84"><a href="#cite_note-84">[84]</a></sup></p>
<h5><span class="mw-headline" id="Howard_Government">Howard Government</span><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=Australian_Broadcasting_Corporation&amp;action=edit&amp;section=16" title="Edit section: Howard Government">edit</a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></h5>
<div class="thumb tright">
<div class="thumbinner" style="width:172px;"><a class="image" href="/wiki/File:Maxine_McKew_Portrait_2007.jpg"><img alt="" class="thumbimage" data-file-height="719" data-file-width="583" height="210" src="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/a/ac/Maxine_McKew_Portrait_2007.jpg/170px-Maxine_McKew_Portrait_2007.jpg" srcset="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/a/ac/Maxine_McKew_Portrait_2007.jpg/255px-Maxine_McKew_Portrait_2007.jpg 1.5x, //upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/a/ac/Maxine_McKew_Portrait_2007.jpg/340px-Maxine_McKew_Portrait_2007.jpg 2x" width="170"/></a>
<div class="thumbcaption">
<div class="magnify"><a class="internal" href="/wiki/File:Maxine_McKew_Portrait_2007.jpg" title="Enlarge"></a></div>
During the <a href="/wiki/Howard_Government" title="Howard Government">Howard Government</a> years, ABC TV's masthead political programs were anchored by Labor affiliated journalists. Lateline host <a href="/wiki/Maxine_McKew" title="Maxine McKew">Maxine McKew</a> (pictured) ran for Labor against Liberal Prime Minister <a href="/wiki/John_Howard" title="John Howard">John Howard</a> in the 2007 Election.</div>
</div>
</div>
<p>For much of the <a href="/wiki/Howard_Government" title="Howard Government">Howard Government</a> years, ABC TV's masthead political programs were anchored by Labor affiliated journalists Kerry O'Brien, <a href="/wiki/Barrie_Cassidy" title="Barrie Cassidy">Barrie Cassidy</a> and <a href="/wiki/Maxine_McKew" title="Maxine McKew">Maxine McKew</a>. <i><a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/7.30_Report" title="7.30 Report">7.30 Report</a></i> and <i><a href="/wiki/Insiders_(TV_program)" title="Insiders (TV program)">Insiders</a></i> were hosted by former Labor staffers Kerry O'Brien and Barrie Cassidy respectively, while the 2007 election saw <i>Lateline</i> host McKew defeat Liberal Prime Minister <a href="/wiki/John_Howard" title="John Howard">John Howard</a> as the Labor candidate for the seat of Bennelong. At that same election, Liberal front bencher <a href="/wiki/Joe_Hockey" title="Joe Hockey">Joe Hockey</a> was challenged unsuccessfully by ABC Sydney News weatherman turned Labor candidate <a href="/wiki/Mike_Bailey_(weatherman)" title="Mike Bailey (weatherman)">Mike Bailey</a> in the Seat of North Sydney.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-85"><a href="#cite_note-85">[85]</a></sup></p>
<p>Of the 1996 prime ministerial Election debates between Opposition Leader <a href="/wiki/John_Howard" title="John Howard">John Howard</a> and Labor Prime Minister <a href="/wiki/Paul_Keating" title="Paul Keating">Paul Keating</a>, Howard later wrote: "I flatly refused to have Kerry O'Brien of the ABC [moderate the debates] because of the way he had handled the second Keating-<a href="/wiki/John_Hewson" title="John Hewson">Hewson</a> debate in 1993" in which O'Brien "went in to bat" for Keating.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-86"><a href="#cite_note-86">[86]</a></sup> Howard went on to win that election. A decade later, the ABC Media Watch program reported that NSW Liberal Senator <a href="/wiki/Concetta_Fierravanti-Wells" title="Concetta Fierravanti-Wells">Concetta Fierravanti-Wells</a> had written to her constituents to say that the ABC had "a collective loathing" of <a href="/wiki/John_Howard" title="John Howard">John Howard</a>.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-87"><a href="#cite_note-87">[87]</a></sup> At the end of the <a href="/wiki/Howard_Government" title="Howard Government">Howard Government</a>'s term in 2007, left-wing political commentator <a href="/wiki/Robert_Manne" title="Robert Manne">Robert Manne</a> wrote in <i>The Monthly</i> that the Howard Government had viewed the broadcaster as being run by "left-wing ideologues" who had "supposedly pushed the agenda of the Left on issues like refugees, the republic, multiculturalism, reconciliation, radical feminism, extreme environmentalism, anti-Americanism, gay rights and so on."<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-NewTeethForAunty_3-1"><a href="#cite_note-NewTeethForAunty-3">[3]</a></sup></p>
<p>Soon after coming to office in 1996, the Howard Government reduced the ABC's operating grants by 10%.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-88"><a href="#cite_note-88">[88]</a></sup> Its appointment of <a href="/wiki/Jonathan_Shier" title="Jonathan Shier">Jonathan Shier</a> to the position of managing director was controversial, for his program of budget cuts, restructuring and the loss of several high-profile personalities and shows.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-89"><a href="#cite_note-89">[89]</a></sup><sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-90"><a href="#cite_note-90">[90]</a></sup> Shier left the position early, on 31 October 2001.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-91"><a href="#cite_note-91">[91]</a></sup> <i><a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/7.30_Report" title="7.30 Report">7.30 Report</a></i> anchor Kerry O'Brien opposed Howard's budget cuts to the ABC, and describes the appointment of Shier as its Managing Director as a manifestation of the "conservative obsession with the ABC as a kind of biased, left-wing culture".<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-92"><a href="#cite_note-92">[92]</a></sup></p>
<p>In Howard's last election, he was defeated in the Seat of Bennelong by Labor candidate Maxine McKew, who had hosted <i>Lateline</i> during the Howard era.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-93"><a href="#cite_note-93">[93]</a></sup> Peter Mares reported for Radio National that "some wags described it as an 'internal promotion', while others said she'd simply moved from the 'media wing' to the 'political wing' of the ALP". Mares consulted ABC journalist turned NSW Liberal MLA <a href="/wiki/Pru_Goward" title="Pru Goward">Pru Goward</a> who said: " I have no doubt there was left-wing bias, I certainly thought it when I was there", while McKew said there was no left wing bias, though "what I detected years ago in the ABC, much more of a collectivist philosophy".<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-94"><a href="#cite_note-94">[94]</a></sup></p>
<h5><span id="Rudd-Gillard-Rudd_Government_(2007-2013)"></span><span class="mw-headline" id="Rudd-Gillard-Rudd_Government_.282007-2013.29">Rudd-Gillard-Rudd Government (2007-2013)</span><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=Australian_Broadcasting_Corporation&amp;action=edit&amp;section=17" title="Edit section: Rudd-Gillard-Rudd Government (2007-2013)">edit</a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></h5>
<p>ABC TV's masthead political programs continued to have strong Labor Party connections through the period. In October 2010, the ABC announced that former Labor staffer Kerry O'Brien would host <i><a href="/wiki/Four_Corners_(Australian_TV_program)" title="Four Corners (Australian TV program)">Four Corners</a></i>, beginning in 2011.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-fourcorners_95-0"><a href="#cite_note-fourcorners-95">[95]</a></sup><sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-fourcornersabconl_96-0"><a href="#cite_note-fourcornersabconl-96">[96]</a></sup> Former Labor staffer <a href="/wiki/Barrie_Cassidy" title="Barrie Cassidy">Barrie Cassidy</a> continued to host the <i>Insiders</i> program. In December 2010, <a href="/wiki/Chris_Uhlmann" title="Chris Uhlmann">Chris Uhlmann</a>, husband of Labor MP <a href="/wiki/Gai_Brodtmann" title="Gai Brodtmann">Gai Brodtmann</a>, was appointed as co-host of the <i><a href="/wiki/7.30" title="7.30">7.30</a></i> current affairs program.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-Report_loses_one_97-0"><a href="#cite_note-Report_loses_one-97">[97]</a></sup> In 2012, Sydney ABC News anchor <a href="/wiki/Juanita_Phillips" title="Juanita Phillips">Juanita Phillips</a> began a relationship with Labor's Minister for Climate Change, <a href="/wiki/Greg_Combet" title="Greg Combet">Greg Combet</a>.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-98"><a href="#cite_note-98">[98]</a></sup><sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-99"><a href="#cite_note-99">[99]</a></sup><sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-100"><a href="#cite_note-100">[100]</a></sup><sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-101"><a href="#cite_note-101">[101]</a></sup></p>
<p>Conservative commentators such as <a href="/wiki/Andrew_Bolt" title="Andrew Bolt">Andrew Bolt</a>,<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-bolt-blog_102-0"><a href="#cite_note-bolt-blog-102">[102]</a></sup> <a href="/wiki/Tim_Blair" title="Tim Blair">Tim Blair</a> and <a href="/wiki/Gerard_Henderson" title="Gerard Henderson">Gerard Henderson</a><sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-bolt-blog_102-1"><a href="#cite_note-bolt-blog-102">[102]</a></sup> accused the ABC of a left-wing bias.</p>
<h5><span id="Abbott-Turnbull_Government_(2013-Present)"></span><span class="mw-headline" id="Abbott-Turnbull_Government_.282013-Present.29">Abbott-Turnbull Government (2013-Present)</span><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=Australian_Broadcasting_Corporation&amp;action=edit&amp;section=18" title="Edit section: Abbott-Turnbull Government (2013-Present)">edit</a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></h5>
<p>Liberal Prime Minister <a href="/wiki/Tony_Abbott" title="Tony Abbott">Tony Abbott</a> perceived the ABC to be left wing and hostile to <a href="/wiki/Abbott_Government" title="Abbott Government">his government</a>, while his successor <a href="/wiki/Malcolm_Turnbull" title="Malcolm Turnbull">Malcolm Turnbull</a> enjoyed better relations with the National Broadcaster. When the ABC co-operated with <i>The Guardian</i> to publish <a href="/wiki/Edward_Snowden" title="Edward Snowden">stolen documents</a> purporting to reveal monitoring of Indonesian officials by Australian spy agencies under the <a href="/wiki/Rudd_Government_(2013)" title="Rudd Government (2013)">Rudd Government</a>, Abbott told 2GB radio: "A lot of people feel at the moment that the ABC instinctively takes everyone's side but Australia's".<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-103"><a href="#cite_note-103">[103]</a></sup><sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-104"><a href="#cite_note-104">[104]</a></sup><sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-105"><a href="#cite_note-105">[105]</a></sup> Abbott reportedly called the <i>Q&amp;A</i> program a "Lefty Lynch Mob".<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-106"><a href="#cite_note-106">[106]</a></sup> When it invited a man convicted of threatening Commonwealth officials to participate in questioning one of his ministers amid a heightened terrorism alert in June 2015, Abbott asked the makers of the program: "whose side are you on?".<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-107"><a href="#cite_note-107">[107]</a></sup><sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-108"><a href="#cite_note-108">[108]</a></sup> The ABC found that there had been an "error of judgement', but repeated the program later in the week, prompting Abbott to say that "heads should roll" over the affair.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-109"><a href="#cite_note-109">[109]</a></sup> Abbott initiated a brief ministerial boycott of the <i>Q&amp;A</i> program following the affair.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-110"><a href="#cite_note-110">[110]</a></sup></p>
<p>The broadcaster was critical of Abbott when he broke an election-eve promise not to make cuts to the ABC, and required 4.6% cuts over five years as part of his "Budget repair" program.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-McNair_111-0"><a href="#cite_note-McNair-111">[111]</a></sup><sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-Farr_112-0"><a href="#cite_note-Farr-112">[112]</a></sup> In early 2015, an internal ABC review of its coverage of <a href="/wiki/Joe_Hockey" title="Joe Hockey">Joe Hockey</a>'s first Budget criticised the post-budget interviews by <i>7:30</i> and <i>Lateline</i>, finding that the interviewers had given the impression of bias.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-113"><a href="#cite_note-113">[113]</a></sup></p>
<p>When Abbott lost the leadership to Turnbull in the <a href="/wiki/Liberal_Party_of_Australia_leadership_spill,_September_2015" title="Liberal Party of Australia leadership spill, September 2015">September 2015 Liberal leadership spill</a>, the hosts of the ABC's political programs spoke in favour of Abbott's demise. <a href="/wiki/Kerry_O%27Brien_(journalist)" title="Kerry O'Brien (journalist)">Kerry O'Brien</a> and <a href="/wiki/Barrie_Cassidy" title="Barrie Cassidy">Barrie Cassidy</a>, hosts respectively of the ABC's flagship weekly current affairs programs <i>Four Corners</i> and <i>Insiders</i>, welcomed the replacement of Abbott by Turnbull,<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-114"><a href="#cite_note-114">[114]</a></sup><sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-115"><a href="#cite_note-115">[115]</a></sup> as did ABC radio commentators <a href="/wiki/Fran_Kelly" title="Fran Kelly">Fran Kelly</a><sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-116"><a href="#cite_note-116">[116]</a></sup> <a href="/wiki/Paul_Bongiorno" title="Paul Bongiorno">Paul Bongiorno</a><sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-117"><a href="#cite_note-117">[117]</a></sup> and <a href="/wiki/Amanda_Vanstone" title="Amanda Vanstone">Amanda Vanstone</a>.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-118"><a href="#cite_note-118">[118]</a></sup> Fairfax and News Limited reported that <a href="/wiki/Leigh_Sales" title="Leigh Sales">Leigh Sales</a>, the host of <i>7.30</i> gave Turnbull an unusually warm first interview following his toppling of Abbott.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-119"><a href="#cite_note-119">[119]</a></sup><sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-120"><a href="#cite_note-120">[120]</a></sup></p>
<p>In a March 2016 interview with ABC Managing Director Mark Scott, <i>Media Watch</i> host Paul Barry examined the question of perceptions of left wing bias at the ABC. Scott noted that while perhaps the ABC was more concerned about gay marriage than about electricity prices, he did not accept the criticism of bias because "a lot of that criticism comes from right wing commentators and they wonder where are the strong right wing commentators on the ABC. We don’t do that kind of journalism. We don’t ask questions about our journalists’ voting pattern and where their ideology are. We look at the journalism that they put to air and we have strong editorial standards..."<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-121"><a href="#cite_note-121">[121]</a></sup> Following the interview, conservative ABC critic Andrew Bolt wrote "How can the man heading our biggest media organisation be so blind to the ABC's unlawful and dangerous Leftist bias?" while former <i>Media Watch</i> host Jonathan Holmes wrote for <i>The Age</i> that this interview indicated that ABC management had failed to recognise a clear problem of left wing bias among some capital city radio presenters.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-122"><a href="#cite_note-122">[122]</a></sup></p>
<p>Over the period, ABC TV and radio hosts advocated strongly in support of same-sex marriage, upon which the wider Australian community and political parties were divided. When the Turnbull Government announced plans for a postal plebiscite on the issue, advocacy for change continued, prompting a call for restraint from the ABC's editorial policy manager Mark Maley.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-123"><a href="#cite_note-123">[123]</a></sup></p>
<p>An interview by ABC presenter Joe O'Brien with Lyle Shelton was the subject of a complaint by the Australian Christian Lobby. Bringing up <a href="/wiki/Ian_Thorpe" title="Ian Thorpe">Ian Thorpe</a>'s swimming achievements, O'Brien asked Shelton "what right do you have to participate in that joy, and take national pride in those achievements, if you now deny him the right to feel like an equal and experience the joy of marriage?"<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-124"><a href="#cite_note-124">[124]</a></sup> In rejecting any perceived bias, the ABC said "It was a 'devil's advocate' question and not inconsistent with standards".<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-125"><a href="#cite_note-125">[125]</a></sup></p>
<h4><span class="mw-headline" id="ABC_journalists_in_politics">ABC journalists in politics</span><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=Australian_Broadcasting_Corporation&amp;action=edit&amp;section=19" title="Edit section: ABC journalists in politics">edit</a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></h4>
<p>A number of former journalists and presenters have moved from positions at the ABC to politics.</p>
<p>State Labor premiers and chief ministers <a href="/wiki/Bob_Carr" title="Bob Carr">Bob Carr</a>,<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-126"><a href="#cite_note-126">[126]</a></sup> <a href="/wiki/Alan_Carpenter" title="Alan Carpenter">Alan Carpenter</a>,<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-127"><a href="#cite_note-127">[127]</a></sup> and <a href="/wiki/Clare_Martin" title="Clare Martin">Clare Martin</a><sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-128"><a href="#cite_note-128">[128]</a></sup> are all former ABC journalists. Other ABC Labor politicians include <a href="/wiki/Mary_Delahunty" title="Mary Delahunty">Mary Delahunty</a>,<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-129"><a href="#cite_note-129">[129]</a></sup> <a href="/wiki/Maxine_McKew" title="Maxine McKew">Maxine McKew</a>,<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-130"><a href="#cite_note-130">[130]</a></sup> <a href="/wiki/Mike_Bailey_(weatherman)" title="Mike Bailey (weatherman)">Mike Bailey</a>, <a href="/wiki/Ian_Baker_(politician)" title="Ian Baker (politician)">Ian Baker</a>, <a href="/wiki/Leon_Bignell" title="Leon Bignell">Leon Bignell</a>, <a href="/wiki/John_Bowler_(politician)" title="John Bowler (politician)">John Bowler</a>, <a href="/wiki/Bob_Debus" title="Bob Debus">Bob Debus</a>, <a href="/wiki/Malarndirri_McCarthy" title="Malarndirri McCarthy">Malarndirri McCarthy</a>, <a href="/wiki/Frank_McGuire_(politician)" title="Frank McGuire (politician)">Frank McGuire</a>, <a href="/wiki/Neville_Oliver" title="Neville Oliver">Neville Oliver</a> and <a href="/wiki/Diana_Warnock" title="Diana Warnock">Diana Warnock</a>. Senior ABC political reporter <a href="/wiki/Kerry_O%27Brien_(journalist)" title="Kerry O'Brien (journalist)">Kerry O'Brien</a> was press secretary to Labor prime minister <a href="/wiki/Gough_Whitlam" title="Gough Whitlam">Gough Whitlam</a> and Labor deputy leader <a href="/wiki/Lionel_Bowen" title="Lionel Bowen">Lionel Bowen</a><sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-131"><a href="#cite_note-131">[131]</a></sup> and <a href="/wiki/Barrie_Cassidy" title="Barrie Cassidy">Barrie Cassidy</a> was press secretary to Labor prime minister <a href="/wiki/Bob_Hawke" title="Bob Hawke">Bob Hawke</a>. <a href="/wiki/Susan_Templeman" title="Susan Templeman">Susan Templeman</a>'s husband, Ron Fuller, is the former Chief of Staff for ABC TV News. Radio National's <a href="/wiki/Phillip_Adams" title="Phillip Adams">Phillip Adams</a> is a former member of the <a href="/wiki/Communist_Party_of_Australia" title="Communist Party of Australia">Communist Party of Australia</a> and the Labor Party, and Melbourne ABC radio's <a href="/wiki/Jon_Faine" title="Jon Faine">Jon Faine</a> is a former member of the Labor Party.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-132"><a href="#cite_note-132">[132]</a></sup></p>
<p>On the Coalition side of politics, <a href="/wiki/Pru_Goward" title="Pru Goward">Pru Goward</a> has served as a Minister in the NSW state Liberal Government,<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-133"><a href="#cite_note-133">[133]</a></sup> <a href="/wiki/Rob_Messenger" title="Rob Messenger">Rob Messenger</a>,<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-134"><a href="#cite_note-134">[134]</a></sup> <a href="/wiki/Peter_Collins_(New_South_Wales_politician)" title="Peter Collins (New South Wales politician)">Peter Collins</a>,<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-fotabc-staff_135-0"><a href="#cite_note-fotabc-staff-135">[135]</a></sup> <a href="/wiki/Eoin_Cameron" title="Eoin Cameron">Eoin Cameron</a>,<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-136"><a href="#cite_note-136">[136]</a></sup> <a href="/wiki/Scott_Emerson" title="Scott Emerson">Scott Emerson</a> and <a href="/wiki/Sarah_Henderson" title="Sarah Henderson">Sarah Henderson</a> all held, or hold, positions at the ABC. Radio National's <i>Counterpoint</i> program is hosted by former Liberal minister <a href="/wiki/Amanda_Vanstone" title="Amanda Vanstone">Amanda Vanstone</a>, who describes herself as "liberal" rather than "conservative".<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-137"><a href="#cite_note-137">[137]</a></sup></p>
<p>Research undertaken by the broadcaster in 2007 indicated that out of a total of 19 former employees moving into party political positions, 10 have joined the Labor Party and nine the Liberal Party.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-138"><a href="#cite_note-138">[138]</a></sup></p>
<h2><span class="mw-headline" id="Services">Services</span><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=Australian_Broadcasting_Corporation&amp;action=edit&amp;section=20" title="Edit section: Services">edit</a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></h2>
<h3><span class="mw-headline" id="Radio">Radio</span><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=Australian_Broadcasting_Corporation&amp;action=edit&amp;section=21" title="Edit section: Radio">edit</a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></h3>
<div class="thumb tright">
<div class="thumbinner" style="width:222px;"><a class="image" href="/wiki/File:ABC_Building_South_Bank.jpg"><img alt="" class="thumbimage" data-file-height="2448" data-file-width="3264" height="165" src="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/5/5e/ABC_Building_South_Bank.jpg/220px-ABC_Building_South_Bank.jpg" srcset="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/5/5e/ABC_Building_South_Bank.jpg/330px-ABC_Building_South_Bank.jpg 1.5x, //upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/5/5e/ABC_Building_South_Bank.jpg/440px-ABC_Building_South_Bank.jpg 2x" width="220"/></a>
<div class="thumbcaption">
<div class="magnify"><a class="internal" href="/wiki/File:ABC_Building_South_Bank.jpg" title="Enlarge"></a></div>
<a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/612_ABC_Brisbane" title="612 ABC Brisbane">ABC Brisbane headquarters in South Bank</a></div>
</div>
</div>
<div class="hatnote navigation-not-searchable" role="note">Main article: <a href="/wiki/ABC_Radio_and_Regional_Content" title="ABC Radio and Regional Content">ABC Radio and Regional Content</a></div>
<p>The ABC operates 54 local radio stations, in addition to four national networks and international service <a href="/wiki/Radio_Australia" title="Radio Australia">Radio Australia</a>. In addition, <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/ABC_DiG" title="ABC DiG">DiG Radio</a> launched on digital platforms in 2002, currently offering three separate stations.</p>
<p><a href="/wiki/ABC_Local_Radio" title="ABC Local Radio">ABC Local Radio</a> is the Corporation's flagship radio station in each broadcast area. There are 54 individual stations, each with a similar format consisting of locally presented light entertainment, news, talk back, music, sport and interviews, in addition to some national programming such as <i>AM</i>, <i>PM</i>, <i><a class="new" href="/w/index.php?title=The_World_Today_(Australian_radio_programme)&amp;action=edit&amp;redlink=1" title="The World Today (Australian radio programme) (page does not exist)">The World Today</a></i>, sporting events and <i>Nightlife</i>.</p>
<p>ABC Grandstand is a live radio sports focused commentary and talk-back program which runs on the Australian Broadcasting Corporation local radio network across Australia and on one digital-only station. The program runs on Saturdays and Sundays, typically from noon or an hour before, until 6 pm.</p>
<p>Double J is aimed at over-30s alternative music listeners. It is owned and operated by the Australian Broadcasting Corporation.</p>
<p>ABC Jazz was launched as a digital only station designed to broadcast a variety of different jazz styles including bebop, acid jazz, cool jazz and contemporary styles of Jazz.</p>
<p>Triple J Unearthed is where artists upload their music and they play and judge it on the channel.</p>
<p>ABC Extra is for special events national Digital Radio channel brings you extra coverage of events and ideas that matter.</p>
<p>ABC Radio Australia is the international radio station.</p>
<p>ABC Country features country style music.</p>
<p><a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/ABC_Radio_National" title="ABC Radio National">ABC Radio National</a> broadcasts more than 60 special interest programmes per week covering a range of topics including music, comedy, book readings, radio dramas, poetry, science, health, the arts, religion, social history and current affairs.</p>
<p><a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/ABC_NewsRadio" title="ABC NewsRadio">ABC NewsRadio</a> is a rolling news service, previously known as the <a href="/wiki/Parliamentary_and_News_Network" title="Parliamentary and News Network">Parliamentary and News Network</a>. The service was established to broadcast federal parliamentary sittings, to relieve the local ABC radio network from this intermittent task, and to provide a news service at other times. The network broadcasts news on a 24/7 format with updates on the quarter-hour. Much of its news content is produced by the ABC itself, however many programmes are relayed from the <a href="/wiki/BBC_World_Service" title="BBC World Service">BBC World Service</a>, <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/National_Public_Radio" title="National Public Radio">NPR</a>, <a href="/wiki/Deutsche_Welle" title="Deutsche Welle">Deutsche Welle</a>, <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Radio_Netherlands" title="Radio Netherlands">Radio Netherlands</a> and <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/CNN_Radio" title="CNN Radio">CNN Radio</a>.</p>
<p><a href="/wiki/ABC_Classic_FM" title="ABC Classic FM">ABC Classic FM</a> was the ABC's first FM radio service. It was originally known simply as "ABC FM", and for a short time<sup class="noprint Inline-Template Template-Fact" style="white-space:nowrap;">[<i><a href="/wiki/Wikipedia:Manual_of_Style/Dates_and_numbers" title="Wikipedia:Manual of Style/Dates and numbers"><span title="This term requires quantification. (April 2013)">quantify</span></a></i>]</sup> "ABC Fine Music". Its format borrowed heavily from community stations that eventually founded the Fine Music Network, as well as <a href="/wiki/BBC_Radio_3" title="BBC Radio 3">BBC Radio 3</a>.</p>
<p><a href="/wiki/Triple_J" title="Triple J">Triple J</a> is the national youth radio network, and broadcasts contemporary alternative and independent music; it is targeted at people aged 18–35. While the network plays music from around the world, it has a strong focus on local artists. Triple J was formerly known as "Double Jay" when it launched in Sydney on 19 January 1975.</p>
<p>ABC Radio broadcasts regular news bulletins across most of its radio stations. Many of these bulletins are heralded by the "<a href="/wiki/Majestic_Fanfare" title="Majestic Fanfare">Majestic Fanfare</a>", written by British composer <a href="/wiki/Charles_Williams_(composer)" title="Charles Williams (composer)">Charles Williams</a> in 1935.</p>
<h3><span class="mw-headline" id="Television">Television</span><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=Australian_Broadcasting_Corporation&amp;action=edit&amp;section=22" title="Edit section: Television">edit</a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></h3>
<div class="hatnote navigation-not-searchable" role="note">Main article: <a href="/wiki/ABC_Television" title="ABC Television">ABC Television</a></div>
<p>The ABC operates 6 national television channels.</p>
<p>ABC is a TV channel that consists of programs of:</p>
<ul>
<li>Art and Culture: Stories I Want To Tell You In Person, The A-Z Of Contemporary Art,</li>
<li>Current Affairs: 7.30, ABC News, Australian Story, Back Roads, Four Corners, Insiders, Landline, Lateline, Media Watch, Q&amp;A, The Drum.</li>
<li>Comedy: Birds of a feather, Growing Up Gracefully, It's A Date, Luke Warm Sex, Shaun Micallef's MAD AS HELL, Utopia</li>
<li>Documentaries and Factual: Antiques Roadshow, Ask The Doctor, Back Roads, Brian Cox: Life Of A Universe, Catalyst, City In The Sky, Compass, David Attenborough's Natural History Museum Alive, Dream Build, Enigma Man: A Stone Age Mystery, Grand Designs, Grand Designs New Zealand, The Checkout, Q&amp;A, Joanna Lumley's India, Mary Berry's Absolute Favourites, Media Watch.</li>
<li>Drama: Agatha Raisin, Cleverman, Death In Paradise, Doc Martin, Father Brown, Happy Valley, Humans, Line Of Duty, Midsomer Murders, Prime Suspect 1973, Pulse</li>
<li>Entertainment: Adam Hills: The Last Leg, Eggheads, Gardening Australia, Grand Designs, Growing Up Grafefully, Hard Quiz, Pointless, QI, Antiques Roadshow, Short Cuts To Glory, The Checkout, The House, You Can't Ask That</li>
<li>Indigenous: Cleverman</li>
<li>Environment: Wild Life At The Zoo, Landline, Gardening Australia</li>
<li>News: 7.30, ABC News, Australian Story, Back Roads, Four Corners, Insiders, Landline, Lateline, Media Watch, Q&amp;A, The Drum, Q&amp;A, Offsiders</li>
<li>Sport: Golf: PGA TOUR Highlights, Offsiders</li>
<li>Special Events</li>
<li>Science: Ask The Doctor, Becoming Superhuman, Brian Cox: Life Of A Universe, Catalyst, Gardening Australia, Humans, Stargazing Live, Todd Sampson's Life On The Line</li>
</ul>
<p>ABC HD has the same programs as ABC but is in <a href="/wiki/High-definition_television" title="High-definition television">high definition</a>.</p>
<p>ABC2 has comedy, drama, documentaries and repeats from ABC.</p>
<p>ABC Me is another TV channel, but with a focus for primary school children, 6–15 years old. It broadcasts a range of genres, including comedy, drama, music, animation, extreme sports, wildlife and news-based programmes.</p>
<p>ABC Kids is a TV channel for children under 6, with educational programs.</p>
<p>ABC NEWS is a 24-hour news channel with news related programs, such as <i><a href="/wiki/News_Breakfast" title="News Breakfast">News Breakfast</a>, <a href="/wiki/Weekend_Breakfast" title="Weekend Breakfast">Weekend Breakfast</a>, ABC News Mornings, <a href="/wiki/ABC_News_at_Noon" title="ABC News at Noon">ABC News at Noon</a>, <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/ABC_News_24" title="ABC News 24">ABC News Afternoons</a>, ABC News — Early Edition, 7.30, Lateline, Insiders, Four Corners, Behind the News, Q&amp;A, Catalyst, Landline, Offsiders, One Plus One, The Business, The Drum, The Quarters, The World, State to State, Capital Hill</i></p>
<h3><span class="mw-headline" id="Studios">Studios</span><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=Australian_Broadcasting_Corporation&amp;action=edit&amp;section=23" title="Edit section: Studios">edit</a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></h3>
<p>The ABC operates <a href="/wiki/ABC_Studios_(Australia)" title="ABC Studios (Australia)">ABC Studios</a>.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-139"><a href="#cite_note-139">[139]</a></sup> <a href="/wiki/ABC_(Australian_TV_channel)" title="ABC (Australian TV channel)">ABC</a>, the Corporation's original television service, receives the bulk of funding for television and shows first-run news, and <a href="/wiki/ABC_Kids_(Australia)" title="ABC Kids (Australia)">ABC Kids</a>.</p>
<h3><span class="mw-headline" id="Online">Online</span><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=Australian_Broadcasting_Corporation&amp;action=edit&amp;section=24" title="Edit section: Online">edit</a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></h3>
<div class="hatnote navigation-not-searchable" role="note">Main article: <a href="/wiki/ABC_Innovation" title="ABC Innovation">ABC Innovation</a></div>
<p>An experimental Multimedia Unit was established in 1995, charged with developing policy for the ABC's work in web publishing.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-abc-90s_24-8"><a href="#cite_note-abc-90s-24">[24]</a></sup> This unit continued until 2000, when the New Media division was formed, bringing together the ABC's online output as a division similar to Television or Radio.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-abc-00s_26-4"><a href="#cite_note-abc-00s-26">[26]</a></sup> The division had over a million pages of material published by late 2003.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-abc-00s_26-5"><a href="#cite_note-abc-00s-26">[26]</a></sup></p>
<p>In 2001 the New Media division became New Media and Digital Services, reflecting the broader remit to develop content for digital platforms such as <a href="/wiki/Digital_television" title="Digital television">digital television</a>. In addition to ABC Online, the division also had responsibility over the ABC's two digital television services, <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Fly_TV" title="Fly TV">Fly TV</a> and the <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/ABC_Kids_channel" title="ABC Kids channel">ABC Kids channel</a>, until their closure in 2003.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-140"><a href="#cite_note-140">[140]</a></sup> In March 2005 the division oversaw the launch of ABC2, a <a href="/wiki/Free-to-air" title="Free-to-air">free-to-air</a> digital television channel, in effect a replacement for ABC Kids and Fly.</p>
<p>In conjunction with the ABC's radio division, New Media and Digital Services implemented the ABC's first <a href="/wiki/Podcast" title="Podcast">podcasts</a> in December 2004. By mid-2006 the ABC had become an international leader in podcasting with over fifty podcast programmes delivering hundreds of thousands of downloads per week,<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-podcasting_141-0"><a href="#cite_note-podcasting-141">[141]</a></sup> including trial video podcasts of <a href="/wiki/The_Chaser%27s_War_on_Everything" title="The Chaser's War on Everything">The Chaser's War on Everything</a> and <a href="/wiki/Triple_j_tv" title="Triple j tv">jtv</a>.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-vodcasting_142-0"><a href="#cite_note-vodcasting-142">[142]</a></sup></p>
<p>In February 2007, the New Media &amp; Digital Services division was dissolved and divided up amongst other areas of the ABC. It was replaced by a new Innovation division, to manage ABC Online and investigate new technologies for the ABC.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-innovation_143-0"><a href="#cite_note-innovation-143">[143]</a></sup> In 2015 the Innovation division was replaced with the Digital Network division.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-144"><a href="#cite_note-144">[144]</a></sup></p>
<h3><span class="mw-headline" id="International">International</span><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=Australian_Broadcasting_Corporation&amp;action=edit&amp;section=25" title="Edit section: International">edit</a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></h3>
<p><a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Australia_Network" title="Australia Network">Australia Network</a>, formerly ABC Asia Pacific, is an international satellite television service operated by the Australian Broadcasting Corporation, funded by advertising and grants from the <a href="/wiki/Department_of_Foreign_Affairs_and_Trade_(Australia)" title="Department of Foreign Affairs and Trade (Australia)">Department of Foreign Affairs and Trade</a>. Aimed at the Asia-Pacific region, the service broadcasts a mixture of English language programming, including general entertainment, sport, and current affairs.</p>
<p><a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/ABC_Radio_Australia" title="ABC Radio Australia">ABC Radio Australia</a> is an international shortwave, satellite and internet radio service with transmissions aimed at East Asia and the <a href="/wiki/Pacific_Islands" title="Pacific Islands">Pacific Islands</a>, although its signals are also audible in many other parts of the world. It features programmes in various languages spoken in these regions, including <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Putonghua" title="Putonghua">Mandarin</a>, <a href="/wiki/Indonesian_language" title="Indonesian language">Indonesian</a>, <a href="/wiki/Vietnamese_language" title="Vietnamese language">Vietnamese</a>, <a href="/wiki/Khmer_language" title="Khmer language">Khmer</a> and <a href="/wiki/Tok_Pisin" title="Tok Pisin">Tok Pisin</a>.</p>
<p>Radio Australia bulletins are also carried on <a href="/wiki/WRN_Broadcast" title="WRN Broadcast">WRN Broadcast</a>, available via satellite in Europe and North America.</p>
<h3><span class="mw-headline" id="Commercial">Commercial</span><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=Australian_Broadcasting_Corporation&amp;action=edit&amp;section=26" title="Edit section: Commercial">edit</a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></h3>
<div class="hatnote navigation-not-searchable" role="note">Main article: <a href="/wiki/ABC_Commercial" title="ABC Commercial">ABC Commercial</a></div>
<p>ABC Commercial is the division of the ABC responsible for pursuing new sources of revenue for the Corporation.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-innovation_143-1"><a href="#cite_note-innovation-143">[143]</a></sup> It is composed of ABC Retail, ABC Consumer Publishing and Content Sales, as well as ABC Resource Hire. ABC retail outlets were established in 1974. All profits from the sale of consumer product and production services return to the Corporation to reinvest in programme-making.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-consumerpub_145-0"><a href="#cite_note-consumerpub-145">[145]</a></sup></p>
<h3><span class="mw-headline" id="Orchestras">Orchestras</span><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=Australian_Broadcasting_Corporation&amp;action=edit&amp;section=27" title="Edit section: Orchestras">edit</a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></h3>
<table class="mbox-small" role="presentation" style="background-color:#f9f9f9;border:1px solid #aaa;color:#000;">
<tr>
<td class="mbox-image">
<div class="center">

</div>
</td>
<td class="mbox-text plainlist" style="line-height:1.1em">

<div>
<div class="mediaContainer" style="width:220px"><audio class="kskin" controls="" data-durationhint="29.960090702948" data-mwprovider="local" data-mwtitle="Charles_Williams,_'Majestic_Fanfare'.ogg" data-startoffset="0" id="mwe_player_2" preload="none" style="width:220px">

<div class="description" style="padding:2px 0 0 0">The original <a href="/wiki/ABC_News_and_Current_Affairs" title="ABC News and Current Affairs">ABC News and Current Affairs</a> theme music. In the mid-1980s ABC Television changed to its own news theme, while the "Majestic Fanfare" is still used for radio news bulletins.</div>
</div>
<hr/></td>
</tr>
<tr>
<td class="mbox-text" colspan="2" style="line-height:1.1em"><span><i>Problems playing this file? See <a href="/wiki/Wikipedia:Media_help" title="Wikipedia:Media help">media help</a>.</i></span></td>
</tr>
</table>
<p>Up until the installation of disc recording equipment in 1935, all content broadcast on the ABC was produced live, including music.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-abc-birth_146-0"><a href="#cite_note-abc-birth-146">[146]</a></sup> For this purpose, the ABC established broadcasting orchestras in each state, and in some centres also employed choruses and dance bands. This became known as the ABC Concert Music Division, which was controlled by the Federal Director of Music – the first of whom was <a href="/wiki/William_G._James" title="William G. James">W. G. James</a>.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-Sametz_147-0"><a href="#cite_note-Sametz-147">[147]</a></sup></p>
<p>There are currently six state symphony orchestras:</p>
<ul>
<li><a href="/wiki/Adelaide_Symphony_Orchestra" title="Adelaide Symphony Orchestra">Adelaide Symphony Orchestra</a></li>
<li><a href="/wiki/Melbourne_Symphony_Orchestra" title="Melbourne Symphony Orchestra">Melbourne Symphony Orchestra</a></li>
<li><a href="/wiki/Queensland_Symphony_Orchestra" title="Queensland Symphony Orchestra">Queensland Symphony Orchestra</a></li>
<li><a href="/wiki/Sydney_Symphony_Orchestra" title="Sydney Symphony Orchestra">Sydney Symphony Orchestra</a></li>
<li><a href="/wiki/Tasmanian_Symphony_Orchestra" title="Tasmanian Symphony Orchestra">Tasmanian Symphony Orchestra</a></li>
<li><a href="/wiki/West_Australian_Symphony_Orchestra" title="West Australian Symphony Orchestra">West Australian Symphony Orchestra</a></li>
</ul>
<p>The orchestras were corporatised in the 1990s,<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-abc-90s_24-9"><a href="#cite_note-abc-90s-24">[24]</a></sup> and were divested into independent companies on 1 January 2007.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-148"><a href="#cite_note-148">[148]</a></sup></p>
<h2><span class="mw-headline" id="Lissajous_curve_logo">Lissajous curve logo</span><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=Australian_Broadcasting_Corporation&amp;action=edit&amp;section=28" title="Edit section: Lissajous curve logo">edit</a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></h2>
<div class="thumb tmulti tright">
<div class="thumbinner" style="width:368px;max-width:368px">
<div class="tsingle" style="float:left;margin:1px;width:182px;max-width:182px">
<div class="thumbimage"><a class="image" href="/wiki/File:ABCTV1975.svg"><img alt="" data-file-height="300" data-file-width="401" height="135" src="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/0/01/ABCTV1975.svg/180px-ABCTV1975.svg.png" srcset="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/0/01/ABCTV1975.svg/270px-ABCTV1975.svg.png 1.5x, //upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/0/01/ABCTV1975.svg/360px-ABCTV1975.svg.png 2x" width="180"/></a></div>
<div class="thumbcaption" style="clear:left">Lissajous curve logo, as it appeared on air from 1975 to 2001 and again from 20 July 2014 to the present day</div>
</div>
<div class="tsingle" style="float:left;margin:1px;width:182px;max-width:182px">
<div class="thumbimage"><a class="image" href="/wiki/File:Lissajous-Figur_1_zu_3_(Oszilloskop).jpg"><img alt="" data-file-height="480" data-file-width="640" height="135" src="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/4/46/Lissajous-Figur_1_zu_3_%28Oszilloskop%29.jpg/180px-Lissajous-Figur_1_zu_3_%28Oszilloskop%29.jpg" srcset="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/4/46/Lissajous-Figur_1_zu_3_%28Oszilloskop%29.jpg/270px-Lissajous-Figur_1_zu_3_%28Oszilloskop%29.jpg 1.5x, //upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/4/46/Lissajous-Figur_1_zu_3_%28Oszilloskop%29.jpg/360px-Lissajous-Figur_1_zu_3_%28Oszilloskop%29.jpg 2x" width="180"/></a></div>
<div class="thumbcaption" style="clear:left">Lissajous figure on an oscilloscope, on which Bill Kennard designed the current logo</div>
</div>
<div style="clear:left"></div>
</div>
</div>
<p>The ABC logo is one of the most recognisable logos in Australia. In the early years of television, the ABC had been using <a href="/wiki/Lissajous_curve" title="Lissajous curve">Lissajous curves</a> as fillers between programmes. In July 1963, the ABC conducted a staff competition to create a new logo for use on television, stationery, publications, microphone badges and ABC vehicles.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-atvh-50s60s_149-0"><a href="#cite_note-atvh-50s60s-149">[149]</a></sup><sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-150"><a href="#cite_note-150">[150]</a></sup> In 1965, ABC graphics designer Bill Kennard, who had been experimenting with telerecording of the <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Cathode_ray_oscilloscope" title="Cathode ray oscilloscope">cathode ray oscilloscope</a> displays, submitted a design which was part of the waveform from an oscilloscope. The letters "ABC" were added to the design and it was adopted as the ABC's official logo. Kennard was presented with <a href="/wiki/Australian_pound" title="Australian pound">£</a>25 for his design.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-atvh-50s60s_149-1"><a href="#cite_note-atvh-50s60s-149">[149]</a></sup></p>
<p>Since its original introduction in 1965, it has been updated several times, including with the introduction of colour television in 1975. The line was thickened to feature colour in the logo. The 1975 logo is the longest-running logo, with a lifespan of 27 years. In 2001, with the introduction of digital television in Australia, ABC Television adopted a modified version of the logo, featuring a silver 3D look and losing the "over and under" design. However, despite the launch of this logo, the 1975 logo is still used by the corporation. In July 2002, to celebrate the ABC's 70th anniversary, the corporation adopted a new logo across all media. This new logo still used the silver 3D colour but reverted to its "over and under" design. In 2014, as part of ABC1's renaming back into "ABC TV", the 1975 logo was brought back to on-air presentation. Despite this, the 2002 silver logo remains in usage by the corporation.</p>
